+Jamison Brereton

1 (192)
Agni
Gr╠еtsamada Bh─Бrgava ┼Ъaunaka, originally ─Ас╣Еgirasa ┼Ъaunahotra
16 verses: jagat─л
This hymn is structured as a series of identificationsтАФof the god Agni with priests, other gods, kin/social relations, qualities, body parts, and so on, with the identifica tion mediated by the quality held in common.
Although the equations may at first seem randomly ordered, in fact they fol low a logical progression. The first ones (vs. 2) identify Agni with human priests. (Priestly identifications are also found extensively in II.5. And for the relationship between particular priests and particular gods, see also the R╠еtugraha hymns I.15, II.36тАУ37.) In the next five verses (3тАУ7) the variety of functions Agni discharges invite identification with a series of gods. Verses 8тАУ9 then set Agni in the web of human relationships, of varying degrees of close kinship. We return to the divine (or semi-divine) world in verses 10тАУ11, but the identifications here link him especially to ritual activity (the R╠еbhus in vs. 10, who are associated with the Third Pressing and who achieved divinity by their ritual feats; the female divinities in vs. 11, who are regularly mentioned in the ─Аpr─л hymns) and prepare for the last section of the hymn (vss. 12тАУ14). The R╠еbhu verse (10) also contains an elaborate pun, while the identification of Agni with three female divinities in verse 11 would surely provoke attention in the audience. AgniтАЩs own ritual service, especially to the gods, provides the subject of verses 12тАУ14. The last p─Бda of this last section (14d) provides a ring with the first verse (1d): тАЬyou were born blazingтАЭ (jaj├▒iс╣гe ┼Ы├║ciс╕е 14d), reprising тАЬyou are born blazingтАЭ (j─Бyase ┼Ы├║ciс╕е 1d), in both cases with a mention of the plants as his source. This neat ring, which closes the series of individual identifications, sets the stage for the climactic verse 15 (before the refrain of 16), which proclaims AgniтАЩs complete superiority throughout heaven and earth.
The identifications are themselves structured by an extraordinary density of rhe torical repetition. Of the sixteen verses, the first fourteen begin with a form of the 2nd-person singular pronoun tv├бm тАЬyou,тАЭ followed by the vocative agne тАЬo Agni.тАЭ In fact fifty-four p─Бdas out of fifty-six open with a 2nd-person singular pronoun, in addition to other pronominal forms scattered in non-initial position. For exam ple, there are seven forms of tva╠Бm in the first verse alone. The fifteenth verse (and the last before the refrain) begins, as usual, with tva╠Бm, but the vocative a╠Бgne is postponed till the opening of the second p─БdaтАФdistracting the formula. As often, rhetorical patterns established earlier in a hymn are varied as the hymn comes to a close, and the change of pattern here draws attention to the climactic contents of verse 15 discussed just above. Though the rhetorical tool, repetition, is a blunt instrument, its effects are powerful.
This rhetorical pattern is especially striking because so many of the pronominal forms are nominatives and therefore unnecessary, since pronominal subjects need not be expressed in Sanskrit. Though some of these nominatives occur in equational sentences (cf. tva╠Бm agn├нd r╠еt─Бyata╠Бс╕е тАЬyou [are] the Agnidh of the one who follows truthтАЭ) where a pronominal forms is often used in place of a copula, a surprising number of these equational sentences also employ a 2nd-person singular copula (asi [e.g., 3a, 5d] or equivalent), rendering a pronominal subject unnecessary. For further
discussion see Jamison (2007: 59тАУ60). Poetics, not grammar, is the driving factor. The effect of this incantatory repetition of тАЬyou, Agni,тАЭ taking place in front of the sacrificial fire on the ritual ground, combined with the sweep of equations identifying Agni with what comes to seem like everything on earth and in heaven, is to concentrate all of the cosmos into this small space, the sacrifical ground, and this single entity, the sacrificial fireтАФindeed making the sacrificial microcosm the equivalent of the macrocosm. The ordering of the identificationsтАФstarting and ending at the sacrifice, but in between ranging through both the divine and human realmsтАФmodels the centrality of the sacrifice and of its focus, the sacred fire. It is a powerful beginning to the maс╣Зс╕Нala and to the Family Books in general.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni For the rhetorical structure of the hymn, see the published introduction.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSovereign of men, Agni, you are born for the days (of sacrifice), pure and all-irradiating, from the waters, from the stones, from trees, and from plural nts.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Su┼Ыukс╣гaс╣Зi = drying up, causing the evaporation of the earth’s moisture; or, it may mean: destroying, consuming; Agni is produced from the waters, either as lightning that accompanies rain or submarine fire; from stones by striking them together; so from trees or wood by attrition; from plural nts, such as bamboo, by mutual friction, causing the conflagration of a forest

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, (are born) throughout the days, you who are eager to blaze here; you (are born) from the waters, you from the stone,
you from the trees, you from the plants, you, men-lord of men, are born blazing.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The only attestation of the desiderative of тИЪ┼Ыuc is this hapax adj. ─Б┼Ыu┼Ыukс╣г├бс╣Зi- тАШeager to blaze hereтАЩ.

+Griffith

THOU, Agni, shining in thy glory through the days, art brought to life from out the waters, from the stone:
From out the forest trees and herbs that grow on ground, thou, Sovran Lord of men art generatad [sic] pure.

+Oldenberg

1 Thou, O Agni, the flaming one, (art born) from out the Heavens 2, thou (art born) from out the Waters and the stone (the flint); thou (art born) from out the forests and the herbs; thou art born bright, O Lord of men, (as belonging) to men 3.

+Geldner

Du, Agni, wirst mit Tagesanbruch geboren, du als Brennlustigster, du wirst aus dem Wasser, du aus dem Stein, du aus den B├дumen, du aus den Pflanzen, du M├дnnerherr wirst rein geboren.

+Grassmann

Durch Flammen wirst geboren du, o Leuchtender, du aus den Wassern, aus dem Wolkenfels hervor, Und aus den B├дumen, aus den Kr├дutern, Agni, auch, der du erstrahlst als M├дnnerherr der M├дnnerschar.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYours Agni, is the office of the Hot─Б, of the Pot─Б, of the с╣Ъtvij, of the Neс╣гс╣н─Б; you are the Agn─лdhra of the devout; yours is the functionof the Pra┼Ы─Бst─Б; you are the Adhvaryu (adhvaryu radhvarayur adhvaram k─Бmayata iti v─Б (Nirukta 1.8) and the Brahm─Б; and the householder in our dwelling.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hot─Б etc.: these are the eight of the sixteen priests employed at very solemn ceremonies; the duty of the Pra┼Ы─Бst─Б is ascribed to the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa, and Brahm─Б is identified with the Br─Бhmaс╣З─Бccahс╣Гsi; Kulluka Bhaс╣нt.a, in his commentary on Manu viii.210 enumerates sixteen priests, in the order and proportion in which they are entitled to share in a dakс╣гiс╣З─Б of a hundred cows, being arranged in four classes, of which the first four are severally the heads, and others subordinate to them, in the same course of succession: 1. Hot─Б, Adhvaryu, Udgat─Б and Brahm─Б, are to have twelve each, or forty-eight in all; 2. Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa, Pratistot─Б, Br─Бhmaс╣З─Бccaс╣Гsi and Prastot─Б, six each, or twenty-four; 3. Accav─Бka, Neс╣гс╣н─Б, ─Аgn─лdhra and Pratihart─Б four each, or sixteen; and 4. Gr─Бvadut, Net─Б, Pot─Б and Subrahmaс╣Зya, three each, or twelve in all; making up the total of one hundred. Thus, the percentages for the four groups are: 48, 24, 16, 12 respectively. R─Бman─Бtha, in his commentary on the Amarako┼Ыa, viii.17 gives the names of 16 priests, but with a few variations: Gr─Бvastut replaces Gr─Бvadut; Prastot─Б, Net─Б and Pot─Б are replaced with Prasth─Бt─Б, Pra┼Ы─Бst─Б and Balaccadaka. In the Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa vii.1, the sixteen priests are enumerated with some variations: Pratistot─Б, Gr─Бvadut, Net─Б and Subrahmaс╣Зya are replaced with Pratiprasthat─Б, Upag─Бt─Б, ─Аtreya and Sadasya. Other priests included in this list are: Gr─Бvastut, Unnet─Б, Subrahmaс╣Зya and the ┼Ъamit─Б (immolator), when a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa. M─Бdhava’s commentary on the Ny─Бya-m─Бla-Vist─Бra of Jaimini, the list of 16 priests, following Kum─Бrila Bhaс╣нt.a includes: 1. Adhvaryu, Prati-prasth─Бt─Б, Neс╣гс╣н─Б, Unnet─Б (ceremonial of the Yajurveda); 2. Brahm─Б, Br─Бhmaс╣З─Бccaс╣Гsi, ─Аgn─лdh, Pot─Б (superintend the whole according to the ritual of the three vedas); 3. Udg─Бt─Б, Prastot─Б, Pratihart─Б, Subrahmaс╣Зya (chant the hymns, especially, S─Бmaveda); 4. Hot─Б, Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa, Acchav─Бka, Gr─Бvastut (repeat the hymns of the с╣Ъc─Б); the head of each class receives the entire dakс╣гiс╣З─Б,or gratuity; the second, one-half; the third, one-third; and the fourth, a quarter

+Jamison Brereton

Yours, Agni, is the office of Hotar; yours that of Potar in its turn; yours that of Neс╣гс╣нar; you are the Agnidh [=Fire-Kindler] of the one who
follows truth.
Yours is the office of Pra┼Ы─Бstar; you act as Adhvaryu; you are both the Brahman-priest and the houselord in our home.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The accent on ├бsi in d presumably results from its contrastive function in the ca тАж ca construction. Curiously Oldenberg does not comment.

Note the two different words for house in gс╣Ыh├бpatiс╕е тАж d├бme, with the former replacing old d├бс╣Гpati-. On these various terms for house-lord, see my forthcoming articles тАЬThe Term gс╣Ыhastha and the (Pre)history of the HouseholderтАЭ (to appear in The Householder in Ancient India: A History of the Gс╣Ыhastha, ed. Patrick Olivelle) and тАЬThe Double Life of gahapatiтАЭ (to appear in a forthcoming Fs.).

+Griffith

Thine is the Herald’s task and Cleanser’s duly timed; Leader art thou, and Kindler for the pious man.
Thou art Director, thou the ministering Priest: thou art the Brahman, Lord and Master in our home.

+Oldenberg

1 To thee, O Agni, belongs the Hotri’s and the Potri’s office exercised at the appointed season; to thee belongs the office of the Neshtri; thou art the Agn├оdh 2 for the righteous. To thee belongs the office of the Pras├вstri; thou actest as an Adhvaryu, and thou art the Brahman and the master of the house in our house 3.

+Geldner

Dir, Agni, kommt das Amt des Hotri zu, dir das Amt des Potri zu seiner Zeit, dir das Amt des Nestri; du bist der Agnidh des Gesetzestreuen. Dir kommt das Amt des Prasastri zu, du wirkst als Adhvaryu. Du bist sowohl der Brahman als auch der Hausherr in unserem Hause.

+Grassmann

Dein ist des Priesters, Agni, dein des L├дuterers rechtm├дssig Amt, des F├╝hrers, dein des Ordnenden; Du bist des Frommen Glutentz├╝nder, opferst gern, und Beter bist du, Hausherr du in unserm Haus.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are Indra, the showerer (of bounties) on the good; you are adorable Viс╣гс╣Зu, the hymned of many; you Brahmaс╣Зaspati, are Brahm─Б, the possessor of riches; you, the author of various (conditions) are associated with wisdom.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, as bull of beings, are Indra; you, wide-going, worthy of homage, are Viс╣гс╣Зu.
You, o lord of the sacred formulation, finder of wealth, are the Brahman [=Formulator]; you, o Apportioner, are accompanied by Plenitude.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition suggest the distracted reading namas├н yaс╕е here and in 10a, which produces 12 syllables for the Jagat─л line but a very bad cadence (4 light syllables), while reading an undistracted form produces a good Triс╣гс╣нubh line. They argue 1) that namas├н ya- is always otherwise distracted in the RV (though it doesnтАЩt otherwise appear in a cadence) and 2) that there are several other similar bad cadences in this hymn (avidhat 7d, 9c). These are good arguments, but I would still favor an undistracted namasy├ас╕е in a Triс╣гс╣нubh line.

Geldner suggests that vidhartaс╕е in d is a predicate voc. I think rather that it signals the absent middle term, the divinity with which Agni is here identified, namely Bhaga. So Oldenberg (SBE). Bhaga is identified as vidhart├бr- in VII.41.2 and is regularly associated with Puraс╣Гdhi.

+Griffith

Hero of Heroes, Agni! Thou art Indra, thou art Visnu of the Mighty Stride, adorable:
Thou, Brahmanaspati, the Brahman finding wealth: thou, O Sustainer, with thy wisdom tendest us.

+Oldenberg

1 Thou, O Agni, art Indra, a bull among (all) beings. Thou art the wide-ruling Vishnu, worthy of adoration. Thou art the Brahman, a gainer of wealth, O Brahmanaspati 2. Thou, O Vidhartri (i. e. who keepest asunder all things), art united with Puramdhi (or the Liberality of the gods) 3.

+Geldner

Du, Agni, bist Indra, der Bulle aller Seienden, du bist der weitschreitende, verehrungsw├╝rdige Vishnu. Du bist der Reichtum findende Hohepriester, o Brahmanaspati. Du, o Austeiler, bist der Purandhi gesellt.

+Grassmann

Du bist, o Agni, Indra, bist der Tapfern Herr, bist Vischnu auch, der hehre, weithinschreitende, Ein Beter, Reichthum schenkend, o Gebetes Herr; du, o Erhalter, bist durch Segensf├╝lle hold.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are the royal Varuс╣Зa, observant of holy vows; you are the adorable Mitra, the destroyer (of foes); you are Aryaman, the protector of the virtuous, whose (liberality) is enjoyed by all; you are a portion (of the sun); be the distributor (of good things), divine (Agni), at our sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whose liberality: liberality is said to be the characteristic of Aryaman, d─Бtс╣Ыtvam caryamс╣Зo liс╣Еgam; you are a portion of the sun: tvam aс╣Г┼Ыaс╕е = forms of the sun, or the ─Аditya, named aс╣Г┼Ыa; You, Agni, are Rudra: tvam rudro asuro maho divaс╕е: asura = ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm nirasit─Б, the expeller of enemies;

Divas = from heaven; or, the giver of strength, asur, balam, tasya dat─Б ─Бditya r┼лpa: a form of ─Бditya, or an ─Бditya

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, whose commandments are steadfast, are King Varuс╣Зa; you, wondrous to be invoked, become Mitra.
You, as the lord of settlements who (offers) a common meal, are
Aryaman; you, apportioning at the ritual distribution, o god, are
Aс╣Г┼Ыa [/Share].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On this vs. see Thieme, Mitra and Aryaman, 83-85.

sambh├║jam in c is analysed by Grassmann as a 1st sg. subj. or injunc. (his тАЬCo.тАЭ) to a thematic aorist and is so rendered by Geldner (тАЬvon dem ich Nutzen haben m├╢chteтАЭ), though he expresses doubts in his n. However, this aor. stem does not otherwise exist: the multiple bhujema forms, apparent optatives in m─Б╠Бprohibitives, are convincingly explained by Hoffmann (Injunk. 95-97) as reanalysed from an expression with the infinitive bhuj├й followed by enclitic 1st ps. pronoun. Moreover, act. forms to this root should mean тАШgive pleasureтАЩ, not тАШderive pleasureтАЩ (cf. bhu├▒jat─л╠Б I.48.5). Oldenberg (Noten) already disputed the verbal interpr. of sambh├║jam, and it is now generally taken as a nominal (so Thieme, Mitra and Aryaman, although in Fremdling [16 n. 2, 105] he takes it as a verb; Hoffmann, Injunk. 96 n. 197; Renou; Scarlatta 358), though Witzel Got┼Н tr. it as a verb, allowing for the nominal possibility in their n. Assuming that sambh├║jam is nominal, the problem is how to fill out the defective rel. cl. y├бsya sambh├║jam. Most supply a verb like тАЬwe eatтАЭ or тАЬwe expect,тАЭ e.g., Scarlatta. тАЬvon dem ich Genuss (erwarte, o. ├д).тАЭ The published translation takes GEN sambh├║jam as a possessive expression: тАЬwhose common meal (it is)тАЭ ├а тАЬwho has a common meal,тАЭ further extended to тАЬwho offers a common meal.тАЭ I find this more satisfying syntactically than the invention of a verb, but it runs into morphological difficulty: by my tr. the meal should be nominative, and if sambh├║jam belongs to a root noun paradigm, it can only be a masc. acc. sg. This forces me into the unhappy position of assuming a root-accented neut. thematic stem -bh├║ja-, which may be unlikely enough morphologically to persuade me to supply a verb to govern the acc.

+Wilson

тАЬYou, Agni, are Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, (the giver) of great wealth to (your) worshipper; these praises are yours; do you, of benevolent power, (admit) our affinity; you, who are prompt to encourage (us), give us good (store of) horses; you, who abound with opulence, are the strength of men.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

[=Maruts].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a has the acc. and dat. appropriate to an expression of giving, but no verb; p─Бda c has the verb (rariс╣гe) but no dative of recipient. The accusatives of gift in the two p─Бdas are formed in parallel: suv─л╠Бr i yam (a), s u v├б┼Ыvi yam (c).The two p─Бdas thus complete each other rhetorically.

In b gn─Б╠Бvaс╕е is morphologically incoherent. By its ending it should be vocative, but since it occupies non-initial position, its accent should preclude that.

Nonetheless, with all the standard interpr. I take it as a voc. An ad hoc explanation could be concocted for its accent – that the following voc. mitramahaс╕е induced accent on the preceding one to support the voc. phrase – but I think too many counter-examples could be adduced. Geldner suggests a word haplology, gn─Б╠Бс╕е gn─Бvaс╕е, but this seems unnecessary and also requires a tr. тАЬyou are (the Wives).тАЭ It is likely instead that the third term in this p─Бda is Tvaс╣гс╣нar from p─Бda a, since he is regularly associated with the Wives of the Gods, and in fact the other attestation of this voc. gn─Б╠Бvaс╕е (I.15.3), correctly accented in p─Бda-initial position, refers to Tvaс╣гс╣нar.

As pointed out by Oldenberg (SBE) and Geldner, the third term in p─Бda c is presumably Ap─Бm Nap─Бt, who is elsewhere called ─Б┼Ыuh├йman-, including 2x in II. The ─Б┼Ыu- in that compound echoes the beginning of ─Б┼Ыu┼Ыukс╣г├бс╣Зiс╕е in 1a, though that form is most probably formed to the desid. stem of тИЪ┼Ыuc with preverb ─Б╠Б, since the -ani-suffix is rather commonly built to desiderative stems and there would be no obvious source of the -s- before the suffix otherwise.

+Griffith

Thou givest strength, as Tvastar, to the worshipper: thou wielding Mitra’s power hast kinship with the Dames.
Thou, urging thy fleet coursers, givest noble steeds: a host of heroes art thou with great store of wealth.

+Oldenberg

Thou, O Agni, being Tvashtri, (grantest) to thy worshipper abundance in heroes. To thee, who art accompanied by the (divine) wives 1, who art great like Mitra, belongs relationship 2. Thou, the quick inciter 3, givest abundance in horses. Thou, rich in wealth, art the host of men 4.

+Grassmann

Als Tvaschtar giebst du, Agni, Kraft dem Huldiger; dir, Freundereicher, sind die G├╢tterfraun verwandt, Du, Rosselenker, schenkest reichen Rossbesitz, bist, Agni, reich wie eine M├дnnerschar an Gut.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are Rudra, the expeller (of foes) from the expanse of heaven; you are the strength of the Maruts; you are supreme over (sacrificial) food; you, who are plural asantly domiciled (in the hall of sacrifice), go with ruddy horses, (fleet as) the wind; as P┼лс╣гan, you cherish, of yours own will, those who offer worship.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, as lord of great heaven, are Rudra; you, as the troop of Maruts, are master of strengthening nourishment [=rain].
You, as luck for livestock, drive with the ruddy winds (as horses); you, as P┼лс╣гan, protect the ones doing honor, in your own person.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the cmpd ┼Ыaс╣Гgay├б-. Wackernagel (AIG II.1.309) classifies it with cmpds with governing first-member prepositions, but ┼Ы├бm, though uninflected, does not function like even the improper prepositions/preverbs like ├бram. He does recognize its singularity (314-15), but keeps it in this category, in which it seems out of place.

+Griffith

Rudra art thou, the Asura of mighty heaven: thou art the Maruts’ host, thou art the Lord of food,
Thou goest with red winds: bliss hast thou in thine home. As Pusan thou thyself protectest worshippers.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are Draviс╣Зod─Бs, to him who honours you; you are the divine Savit─Б, the possessor of precious things; protector of men, you are Bhaga, and rule over wealth; you are the cherisher of him who worships you in his dwelling.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, are Wealth-Giver to the preparer (of the offering); you, as the conferrer of treasure, are god Savitar.
You, lord of men, as Bhaga [/Fortune] are master of goods; you are a protector in the house of him who has done you honor.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda d has another bad cadence: te (├б)vidhat, with 4 light syllables, assuming the normal shortening of -e before vowel. The same cadence is found in 9c. I would be inclined to follow Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition in seeing this irregular cadence as characteristic of this particular hymn (see also 3b, 10a), save for the fact that ├бvidhat shows a remarkable tendency to position itself in bad cadences: see II.26.4, VIII.23.21, 27.15, 61.9. As Ian Hollenbaugh points out to me, Arnold (p.129, ┬з169.vi) suggests reading ─Б╠Бvidhat with long augment. Though in all cases the Saс╣Гhit─Б text transmits either short ├б or deleted abhinihita (├б) and the Pp analyzes it as a in all cases, this seems a reasonable explanation - despite OldenbergтАЩs dismissive тАЬrecht zweifelhaft.тАЭ There is a tendency to lengthen vowels before elements beginning with v, not only the augment, but preverbs, and 1st cmpd. members, presumably spreading from forms that originally began *Hv. In most of the other occurrences of ├бvidhat (I.136.5, VI.54.4, IX.114.1) the augment has coalesced with a preceding a-vowel and its weight is therefore unrecoverable. Only in X.83.1 do we find an ├бvidhat that is not improved by a heavy reading: it occurs in the break after an early caesura. But even here ─Б╠Бvidhat is a possible reading. Though тПС тПС - is the most preferred break, - тПС - is the next most common.

Giver of wealth art thou to him who honours thee; thou art God Savitar, granter of precious things.
As Bhaga, Lord of men! thou rulest over wealth, and guardest in his house him who hath served thee well.

Thou, O Agni, art a giver of wealth to him who does service to thee 1; thou art the god Savitri, a bestower of treasures. Thou, being Bhaga, O lord of men, rulest over wealth. Thou art a protector in his house to him who has worshipped thee. 2.

Du, Agni, bist der Sch├дtzespender f├╝r den, der dir dient; du bist Gott Savitri, der Sch├дtze bringt, Du, o F├╝rst, verf├╝gst als Bhaga ├╝ber das Gut, du bist im Hause der Sch├╝tzer des, der dir willf├дhrig war.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe people adore you, Agni, the protector of the people in their dwellings; they propitiate you as a benevolent sovereign; leader of a radiant host, you are lord over all offerings; you are the distributor of tens, and hundreds, and thousands (of good things).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Toward you, Agni, as clanlord in the house do the clans stretch out straightтАФtoward you, the king, easy to find.
You, lovely-faced one, are lord over all; you are the counter(part) to thousands, hundreds, tens.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Here and in 15a I take pr├бti (+/- copula) + ACC. as an expression similar to pratim─Б╠Бna- + GEN, meaning тАШbe a counterpart toтАЩ.

For с╣Ы├▒jate here, see the fuller expression with instr. in the next hymn, II.2.5.

+Griffith

To thee, the people’s Lord within the house, the folk press forward to their King most graciously inclined.
Lord of the lovely look, all things belong to thee: ten, hundred, yea, a thousand are outweighed by thee.

+Oldenberg

Towards thee, in the house, the lord of the clan, O Agni, the clans strive, towards thee, the bounteous king. Thou with the beautiful face possessest all things. Thou art equal to thousands, to hundreds, to ten (of others).

+Geldner

Dir, Agni, dem Clanf├╝rsten, lassen die Clangenossen im Hause den Vortritt, dir dem zug├дnglichen K├╢nig. Du, sch├╢n von Aussehen, bist Herr ├╝ber alles; du wiegst Tausende, Hunderte, Zehn auf.

+Grassmann

Nach dir, o Agni, der im Hause Stammherr ist, dem gn├дd’gen K├╢nig, streben alle St├дmme hin; Du, sch├╢n von Antlitz, herrschest ├╝ber alles Gut, du wiegest auf an zehn mal hundert Tausende.

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдореНрдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдиреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдирд░реЛрдиреЗрддрд╛рд░реЛрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рднрд┐рд░реЗрд╖рдгрд╕рд╛рдзрдиреИрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЧреИрд░реНрдпрдЬрдиреНрддрдЗрддрд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рдкрд┐рддреГрд╡рддреН рдкрд╛- рд▓рдирд╛рдпрдпрдЬрдиреНрддрдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рддрдерд╛рддрдиреВрд░реБрдЪрдВрд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреНрджреАрдкрдХрдВрд╢рд░реАрд░реЗрд╖реБрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╛рддреНрдордирд╛рддреНрд╡рдореНрднреНрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдпрднреНрд░рд╛рддреГрддреНрд╡рд╛- рдпрд╕реМрднреНрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╢рдореНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордирд╛рдореИрддрддреН рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдпрдЬрдиреНрддрдЗрддрд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рдпрджреНрд╡реЛрднрдпрддреНрд░рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгреЗрдирд╛рд╡рд┐рдзрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдиреЗрдирд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рд╣реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдирд░рд╕реНрддреЗрддреНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЕрд╡рд┐рдзрддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдпрддреНрд╡рдореНрдкреБрддреНрд░реЛрднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╡рддреНрдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рддрдерд╛рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рдЦрд╛рд╕- рдорд╛рдирдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдЦрд┐рд╡рджреНрдзрд┐рддрдХрд╛рд░реАрд╕реБрд╢реЗрд╡рдГ рд╢реЗрд╡рдЗрддрд┐рд╕реБрдЦрдирд╛рдо рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░реАрд╕рдиреН рдЖрдзреГрд╖рдГ рдЖрдзрд░реНрд╖рдХрд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдкрд╛рд╕рд┐- рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд┐ рдкрд┐рддреГрддреНрд╡рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрдкрд┐рддреГрддреНрд╡реЗрдирднреНрд░рд╛рддреГрддреНрд╡рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрднреНрд░рд╛рддреГрддреНрд╡реЗрдирдкреБрддреНрд░рддреНрд╡рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрдкреБрддреНрд░рддреНрд╡рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдпрдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпреЛрднрд╡- рд╕рд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдгрд░рдХреНрд╖рд╕реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее реп рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Devout) men (worship) you, Agni, as a father, with sacred rites; they (cherish) you, who are the illumination of the body, with acts (of kindness), as a brother; you are as a son to him who propitiates you; and you protect us, a faithful and firm friend.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

To you, Agni, as father, (do) men (approach) with their desiresтАФto you, for brotherhood, (do they approach) with their (ritual) labor, you who are bright in body.
You become the son of him who has done you honor; you as
affectionate comradeтАФprotect (him) from assault.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is tempting to take iс╣гс╣н├нbhiс╕е as тАШwith sacrificesтАЩ, parallel to ┼Ы├бmy─Б тАШwith ritual laborтАЩ in the next p─Бda. So Oldenberg (SBE), though he gave it up reluctantly in the Noten.

Unfortunately тАШsacrificeтАЩ is accented ├нс╣гti-, against iс╣гс╣н├н- тАШdesireтАЩ, and so perhaps the best one can do is suggest a secondary pun (so Scarlatta 455). On the other hand, on the assumption that all -t├н-stems began with suffixal accent and that the root accent found in some Vedic -ti-stems is secondary (see Lundquist 2015, -ti-stems), this may be a relic of suffix-accented *iс╣гс╣н├н-тАШsacrificeтАЩ, which has not yet undergone accent retraction. It is worth noting that root-accented ├нс╣гс╣нi- is found only in I and X.

On the cadence in 9 see remarks on 7b.

+Griffith

Agni, men seek thee as a Father with their prayers, win thee, bright-formed, to brotherhood with holy act.
Thou art a Son to him who duly worships thee, and as a trusty Friend thou guardest from attack.

+Oldenberg

Thee, O Agni, men (make) their father by their sacrifices 1; thee who shinest with thy body they (invite) to brotherhood by their (sacrificial) work. Thou becomest a son to him who has worshipped thee. As a kind friend thou protectest against attack.

+Geldner

Zu dir, Agni, als ihrem Vater kommen die M├дnner mit ihren W├╝nschen, zu dir, den am Leib gl├дnzenden mit Opferdienst, auf da├Я du ihr Bruder seiest. Du bist der Sohn dessen, der dir willf├дhrig war; du sch├╝tzest als liebreicher Freund vor Unbill.

+Grassmann

Dich als den Vater gehn die M├дnner heischend an, des Eifers voll, dich gl├дnzenden, um Br├╝derschaft, Ein Sohn, o Agni, bist du dem, der dich verehrt, ein holder Freund und sch├╝tzest ihn vor Ungemach.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are (ever) resplendent, and are to be glorified when present; you are lord over all renowned food and riches; you shine brightly, and you consume (the oblation) for him who offers it; you are the especial accomplisher of the sacrifice, and bestower (of its rewards).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Resplendent: tvam agna с╣Ыbhuс╕е, tvam. v─Бjasya ─л┼Ыiс╣гe: с╣Ыbhu = bh─Бsam─Бnaс╕е, shining;

V─Бjasya = annasya, of food

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, as [R╠еbhu/] the craftsman at hand, are to be rendered homage; you are master of the cattle-rich prize [/V─Бja], of wealth. You radiate widely [/(are) Vibhvan]: burn through to giving! You seek to carve up and to stretch out the sacrifice.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the cadence in p─Бda a, see comm. ad 3b.

As Oldenberg (SBE) already pointed out, the first three p─Бdas refer to the three с╣Ъbhus and pun on their names: с╣Ыbh├║- тАШcraftsman / с╣ЪbhuтАЩ in a, v─Б╠Бja- тАШprize / V─БjaтАЩ in b, and v├н bh─Бsi тАШyou radiate / VibhvanтАЩ in c.

In c dakс╣гi is surely a -si impv. to тИЪdah тАШburnтАЩ and should be separated from the identical form in I.141.8, for which see the comm. ad loc. Geldner, however, takes dakс╣гi here to тИЪdakс╣г.

The form vi┼Ы├нkс╣гu- in d is taken by Grassmann as belonging to the desid. of тИЪ┼Ыak and meaning тАШgerne Gut austheilendтАЩ, which seems unacceptably distant from both the root meaning of тИЪ┼Ыak and the function of the desiderative. Moreover, тИЪ┼Ыak is not otherwise attested with v├н except, supposedly, in the similar form v├н ┼Ыikс╣гa IV.35.3 (for which see below). Geldner tr. тАЬdu bist der Pr├╝fer,тАЭ Renou тАЬtu es celui que si met ├а l’oeuvre diversementтАЭ; neither discusses the form or its root affiliation, and one can only assume they follow the assignment to тИЪ┼Ыak, though exactly how is unclear. Oldenberg (SBE) suggested an appealing alternative, interpreting it as built to the desid. of тИЪ┼Ыas тАШcutтАЩ, which is primarily found with v├н – an idea I find eminently worthy of revival.

This may also be the view of Witzel Got┼Н, who tr. тАЬDu bist williger Verteiler,тАЭ again without disc., so they may in fact simply reproduce GrassmannтАЩs understanding of the semantics. Oldenberg does not sketch out the morphology, but it presumably rests on *┼Ыi-┼Ыs-su-, with zerograde root and simplification of the medial sibilant cluster ┼Ыss arising from the two radical sibilants and the desiderative suffix. The finite verb v├н ┼Ыikс╣гa in IV.35.3 (also a с╣Ъbhus context) belongs here as well. Heenen (Desid., 232-33) mentions this possibility though without great enthusiasm (тАЬLa possiblit├й тАж nтАЩest pas exclueтАЭ).

The published translation тАЬseek to carve up and to stretch out the sacrificeтАЭ implies that ─Бt├бniс╕е is desiderative. This was not meant, and the tr. should perhaps be emended to тАЬseek to carve up the sacrifice, as the one who stretches it outтАЭ or тАЬтАж as you stretch it out.тАЭ

+Griffith

A Rbhu art thou, Agni, near to be adored thou art the Sovran Lord of foodful spoil and wealth.
Thou shinest brightly forth, thou burnest to bestow: pervading sacrifice, thou lendest us thine help.

+Oldenberg

Thou, O Agni, art Ribhu, to be adored when near. Thou rulest over strength 1, over wealth rich in food. Thou shinest 2, thou burnest for the sake of giving (wealth). Thou art a hewer 3, an expander of sacrifice.

+Geldner

Du, Agni, bist Ribhu, vor dem man zu seiner Zeit sich verbeugen mu├Я; du verf├╝gst ├╝ber den Siegergewinn, ├╝ber Reichtum an Vieh. Du erstrahlst; sei bereit zu schenken; du bist der Pr├╝fer, wenn du das Opfer ausrichtest.

+Grassmann

O Agni, Ribhu bist du, hier verehrungswerth, und dein ist Labung, dein auch nahrungsreiches Gut; Du leuchtest hell, entbrenne nun zum Schenken auch; du spendest gerne, wenn das Opfer du durchstrahlst.

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рджреЗрд╡ рддреНрд╡рдиреНрджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖реЗрд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрддреНрддрд╡рддреЗрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐рд░рдЦрдгреНрдбрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд╕рд┐ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрджреАрдирд╛рднреВрдорд┐- рд░рд╕рд┐ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рддреНрд╡рдВрд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рднрд╛рд░рддреАрднрд░рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреАрд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рд╕рддреАрдЧрд┐рд░рд╛рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡- рд░реНрдзрд╕реЗрдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзреЛрднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рддреНрд╡рдВрд╢рддрд╣рд┐рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдорд╢рдмреНрджрдГрдХрд╛рд▓реЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ рдЕрдкрд░рд┐рдорд┐рддрдХрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛ рдЗрд│рд╛ рднреВрдорд┐рд░- рд╕рд┐ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реАрд╕рддреАрджрдХреНрд╖рд╕реЗрджрд╛рдирд╛рдпрд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рддрд┐рдЩрдЙрддреНрддрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рджрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ рддрдерд╛рд╣реЗрд╡рд╕реБрдкрддреЗрдзрдирдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдкрд╛- рдкрд╛рджреЗрд░реНрд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рддреНрд╡рдВрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА рд╕рд░рдгрд╡рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛рдпрдГ рддрддреНрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреАрдПрддрдиреНрдирд┐рдпрд╛рдордХрд╛рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдорд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рд╛рдЧрд╕рд┐ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛- рдпреВрдирд╛рдВрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреНрдпреЛрднрд╛рд░рддреАрд│рд╛рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛрджреЗрд╡реНрдпрдГрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдЕрдкрд┐рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡реЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее резрез рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, divine Agni, are Aditi to the donor of the oblation; you are Hot─Б and Bh─Бrat─л, and thive by praise; you are Iс╕╖─Б of a hundred winters to him who makes you gifts; you, lord of wealth, are the destroyer of Vс╣Ыtra, Sarasvat─л.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Iс╕╖─Б of a hundred winters: tvam iс╕╖─Б;

┼Ъatahim─Бsi = the earth of unlimited duration, aparimitak─Бla bh┼лmiс╕е; destroyer of Vс╣Ыtra: vс╣Ыtrah─Б = destroyer of sin

+Jamison Brereton

You, god Agni, are Aditi for the pious; you, as Hotr─Б Bh─Бrat─л, are strengthened by song.
You are Iс╕Н─Б, bestowing a hundred winters in return for skill; you, o lord of goods, as obstacle-smasher, are Sarasvat─л.

+Griffith

Thou, God, art Aditi to him who offers gifts: thou, Hotri, Bharati, art strengthened by the song.
Thou art the hundred-wintered Ila to give strength, Lord of Wealth! Vrtra-slayer and Sarasvati.

+Oldenberg

+Geldner

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen, well-cherished Agni, you are (the giver of) excellent food; in your desirable and delightful hues, beauties (abound) you (are) food; (you are) the transporter (beyond sin); you are mighty; you are wealth; you are manifold, and everhwhere diffused.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, when well kept, are highest vigor. In your coveted color there are beauties in sight.
You are the prize, furthering and lofty; you are wealth, ample, broad on all sides.

+Griffith

Thou, Agni, cherished well, art highest vital power; in thy delightful hue are glories visible.
Thou art the lofty might that furthers each design: thou art wealth manifold, diffused on every side.

+Oldenberg

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe ─Аdityas have made you, Agni, their mouth; the pure (deities) have made you, Kavi, their tongue; the (gods), the givers of wealth, depdn upon you at sacrifices; they eat the offered oblation through you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, did the ─Аdityas make their mouth; you did the pure ones make their tongue, o poet.
You do the Gift-Escorts escort in the ceremonies; in you do the gods eat the poured oblation.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The relevant construction in d is probably tv├й тАж ─Б╠Бhutam тАЬpoured into you,тАЭ as it is in the even further distracted identical phrase in 14ab. The tr. of 13d should be corrected to тАЬthe gods eat the oblation poured into you.тАЭ

+Griffith

Thee, Agni, have the Adityas taken as their mouth; the Bright Ones have made thee, O Sage, to be their tongue.
They who love offerings cling to thee at solemn rites: by thee the Gods devour the duly offered food.

+Oldenberg

The ├Вdityas have made thee, O Agni, their mouth; the bright ones have made thee their tongue, O Sage. The R├вti-s├вk gods (i. e. the ‘bounteous’ gods) accompany thee at the sacrifices. In thee the gods eat the offering which is offered to them.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll the benignant immortal gods eat the offered oblation through you, as their mouth; mortals taste the flavour (of all viands) through you; you are born pure the embryo of plural nts.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Corn and other grains ripen by the heat of the sun or fire; the text has ┼Ыuci, pure; this is interpreted as vasu, being the abode of all: sarveс╣г─Бm niv─Бsabh┼лtaс╕е san

+Jamison Brereton

O Agni, through your mouth do all the undeceptive immortals, the gods, eat the oblation poured into you.
With you the mortals sweeten their pressed drink. You, as embryo of the plants, were born blazing.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half-verse is simply a rather crudely exploded version of 13d (also found in I.94.3), with tv├й moved to front of first p─Бda and the second p─Бda otherwise intact. See Bloomfield’s withering scorn.

+Griffith

By thee, O Agni, all the Immortal guileless Gods eat with thy mouth the oblation that is offered them.
By thee do mortal men give sweetness to their drink. Bright art thou born, the embryo of the plants of earth.

+Oldenberg

In thee, O Agni, with (thy) mouth 1 all the guileless 2 immortal gods eat the offering which is offered to them. Through thee the mortals taste their drink. Thou hast been born, the bright one, as the child of the plants.

+Geldner

In dir, Agni, verzehren all die Unsterblichen, die Truglosen, durch deinen Mund die G├╢tter die geopferte Spende. Durch dich lassen sich die Sterblichen ihr Tr├дnklein schmecken. Du bist als Leibesfrucht der Pflanzen rein geboren worden.

+Grassmann

Dir sind, o Agni, alle G├╢tter wohlgesinnt, mit deinem Mund verzehren sie den Opfertrank; Durch dich versch├╢nen ihr Gebr├дu die Sterblichen; du wirst geboren leuchtend als der Pflanzen Spross.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou are associated, Agni, by your vigour, with those (gods); divine, well-born Agni, you exceed (them in strength); for the (sacrificial) food that is here prepared is, by your power, subsequently diffused through both regions, heaven and earth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You are both equal and a counter(part) to these by your might, and, o Agni, well-born god, you surpass them,
since your strengthening nourishment here extends in its greatness through heaven and earth, through both world-halves.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On pr├бti тАж asi, see comm. ad 8d. As far as I can determine, this is the only occurrence of s├бm тИЪas in the RV and, rather than meaning something like тАШbe togetherтАЩ, it seems to have an idiomatic meaning like prati + ACC, тАШbe equal toтАЩ (as if to sam├б- vel sim.).

On the word order in p─Бda c, see comm. ad VI.15.14.

+Griffith

With these thou art united, Agni; yea thou, God of noble birth, surpassest them in majesty,
Which, through the power of good, here spreads abroad from thee, diffused through both the worlds, throughout the earth and heaven.

+Oldenberg

1 Thou art united with them and equal to them in strength, O well-born Agni, nay, thou surpassest them, O god, when thy power 2 has expanded here in its greatness over Heaven and Earth, over both worlds.

+Geldner

Du bist diese alle zusammen und wiegst sie an Gr├╢├Яe auf und ├╝berragst sie noch, du edelgeborener Gott Agni, wenn sich deine Kraft hier in voller Gr├╢├Яe entfaltet, ├╝ber Himmel und Erde, ├╝ber beide Rodasi.

+Grassmann

Gleich bist du diesen, ebenb├╝rtig auch an Macht, ja, ├╝bertriffst sie, Agni, sch├╢ngeborner Gott; Als hier das Lastross herrlich dir ger├╝stet war, erf├╝lltest Erd’ und Himmel du, das Weltenpaar.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe pious are they who present, as a gift, to the reciters of your praises, an excellent cow and an excellent horse; do you, Agni, lead both us and them to the best of abodes, (or heaven), that we and our worthy descendants may repeat the solemn prayer to you at the sacrifice.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The patronsтАФthose who dispatch to the praisers a gift tipped with cows and ornamented with horses, o AgniтАФ
lead both us and them forth to a better state. тАУ May we speak loftily at the ritual distribution, in possession of good heroes.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the function or position of h├н, though the latter question is more tractable.

+Griffith

The princely worshippers who send to those who sing thy praise, O Agni, guerdon graced with kine and steeds,-
Lead thou both these and us forward to higher bliss. With brave men in the assembly may we speak aloud.

+Oldenberg

The liberal lords who pour out, O Agni, over thy praisers gifts at the head of which there are cows 1, the ornament of which are horses: lead both ourselves and them to welfare. May we speak loud in the assembly 2, rich in valiant men.
